  <span id="freeText1940509345080014768" style="display:none">*ARC received from Netgalley, in exchange for an honest review*<br /><br />Kudos to you, Amy A. Bartol, because you have done what very few are capable of... making me love a love triangle. I dove into this book expecting greatness and I was not disappointed. I didn't think it was possible, but I completely fell in love with Kyon. He won my heart with his devotion and loyalty. He was still crazy and blood hungry, but he wouldn't let anyone harm Kricket and I loved him for it. Trey.. oh Trey, he really let me down with the decisions he made throughout the book. Although I know he loved Kricket, he left me no choice, but to switch teams. Kricket was so strong and smart, even though people were trying to kill her and betraying her left and right. The ending both broke my heart and made me really happy. I loved this book.</span>

<div id="review_1373933416" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1373933416" />
    <a title="Christy LoveOfBooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1390723-christy-loveofbooks"><img alt="Christy LoveOfBooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472349981p2/1390723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1373933416?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy LoveOfBooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy LoveOfBooks" href="/user/show/1390723-christy-loveofbooks">Christy LoveOfBooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25277389-darken-the-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1390723-christy-loveofbooks?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1390723-christy-loveofbooks?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1390723-christy-loveofbooks?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1390723-christy-loveofbooks?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1390723-christy-loveofbooks?shelf=favorites-of-2015">favorites-of-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1373933416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6685743932357757964"><br/>Wow, I don’t know what to say ...<br/><br/>I fell so deeply in love with this first two books, so I’ll be honest, I was afraid to read <strong>Darken the Stars</strong>. What if it turned out to be a total dud? I would be <em>crushed</em>. I had absolutely nothing to be scared of though. This book is <em>everything</em>!<br/><br/>This book is buried deep into my little black heart for an abundance of reasons, but I don’t feel like I can come close to adequately explaining exactly why, especially without giving spoilers. What it mainly comes down to,</span>
  <span id="freeText6685743932357757964" style="display:none"><br />Wow, I don’t know what to say ...<br /><br />I fell so deeply in love with this first two books, so I’ll be honest, I was afraid to read <strong>Darken the Stars</strong>. What if it turned out to be a total dud? I would be <em>crushed</em>. I had absolutely nothing to be scared of though. This book is <em>everything</em>!<br /><br />This book is buried deep into my little black heart for an abundance of reasons, but I don’t feel like I can come close to adequately explaining exactly why, especially without giving spoilers. What it mainly comes down to, though, is it made me <em>feel</em>. I felt such a wide range of emotions. Not just little flutters here and there, no, I’m talking strong tidal waves of them. The intensity of them drove me crazy sometimes, especially when it came to Kyon, but lordy, did I ever love it like you wouldn’t believe.<br /><br />Kricket has been consistently wonderful the entire series, but in this book, she was so much more. I love this girl and connected with her in so, <em>so</em> many ways! I’m <em>extremely</em> proud of the woman she became and the tough decisions she made. She’s a heroine that will stick with me for many years to come.<br /><br />This isn’t <em>as</em> action packed as the previous book, but that’s perfectly fine. It was more of a chess game with power moves and betrayal, which can be just as deadly. I swear, <strong>Darken the Stars</strong> went just how I would’ve wanted it to.<br /><br />With every book in this series, I’ve gone back and reread the last few chapters after I finished. I can’t let go! With <strong>Darken the Stars</strong>, I read the last chapter and epilogue several times and it still had a major effect on me every time. There were definitely tears involved.<br /><br />As of now, I don’t know whether there will be a fourth book or not. If not, I’m reluctantly at ease with the way it ended. However, I need more! There’s still so much more that can be explored. Either way, I will be rereading this series over and over, far into the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6685743932357757964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1394285784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1394285784" />
    <a title="Brenda A" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9873129-brenda-a"><img alt="Brenda A" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555296245p2/9873129.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1394285784?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenda A" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenda A" href="/user/show/9873129-brenda-a">Brenda A</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9873129-brenda-a?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1394285784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10882471671962597541">(I received this from NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.)<br/><br/><br/>This is utterly, despicably repulsive. I can't believe that this is a book that has more than 1700 reviews with an average rating of 4.08. I can't <i>fathom</i> how this is considered a successful love story, or how people can rate this so highly.<br/><br/>This is <b>abuse</b> and <b>torture</b> disguised as a love story. This is one man after another physically harming the main character, and her accepting all of it as regular treatment. <br/><br/>Within the first 10 pa</span>
  <span id="freeText10882471671962597541" style="display:none">(I received this from NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.)<br /><br /><br />This is utterly, despicably repulsive. I can't believe that this is a book that has more than 1700 reviews with an average rating of 4.08. I can't <i>fathom</i> how this is considered a successful love story, or how people can rate this so highly.<br /><br />This is <b>abuse</b> and <b>torture</b> disguised as a love story. This is one man after another physically harming the main character, and her accepting all of it as regular treatment. <br /><br />Within the first 10 pages, Kyon is assaulting Kricket. He is forcing himself on her, kissing her and pressing her to his body despite her trying to break away. She bites on his lip hard enough to draw blood and tries to kick him in the balls, and he manages to subdue her. <b>Right away we are shown her saying no, and Kyon disregarding her.</b><br /><br />Within the first 10 pages, Kyon is drowning Kricket to make her submit to him:<br /><br /><blockquote> Kyon's fist tightens again. I'm thrust under the water and held down. The lack of oxygen makes my lungs feel like they'll explode at any second. I panic. Every cell of my body fights for life, except for a small part of me, which is tempted to succumb to the madness of the moment. </blockquote><br /><br />He makes it clear that he has no problem sexually dominating her and also beating compliance into her:<br /><br /><blockquote>"Right now I insist upon your obedience." A wave crashes into my back, pushing me against his chest. I clutch his shoulders and try to steady myself in the water. His hands move from the front of my nightgown to my waist. When the next wave pushes me forward, my breasts press against his chest, and his expression changes from anger to desire. He leans near; his rough cheek rubs against my much softer skin.<br />"I brought you here to hurt you," Kyon murmurs, the timbre of his voice rumbles through his chest into mine. His words make my heart squeeze tight."</blockquote><br /><br />He continuously forces himself on her:<br /><br /><i>"I want this." His nose skims up my throat in an intimate caress.<br />"I don't," I growl between my teeth."</i><br />-------------------------------------<br /><i>My muscles go rigid. Kyon kisses my hair and snuggles tight against me. I begin to struggle and try to pull away from him.<br />"Don't move."<br />"I don't want you to touch me."<br />"I don't care what you want. This is what I want. You need to know that I'm the only person to whom you can turn." </i><br />-------------------------------------<br /><i>"Kyon!"<br />His deep voice murmurs, "I like to hear you wake with my name on your lips." With his shoulders resting against plump, white pillows, Kyon's blue eyes hood as he continues to stare at me. He moves his hand along my hair, stroking me like a favorite pet. </i><br />-------------------------------------<br /><i>"You belong to me. I won't let you go--not ever." </i><br />-------------------------------------<br /><br />His controlling behavior comes around again to make sure that Kricket's body is not hers. She must do as he says:<br /><br /><b>His eyes skim over me slowly, lingering on my breasts in a way that makes me pull the sheet closer. <br />"You don't have to wear anything. We're alone here." </b><br />------------------------------------<br /><b>I slide over to that side of the mattress. When my feet touch the floor, I hold the sheet to me and walk in that direction. I'm halted by a firm tug on the tail of my sheet. Looking over my shoulder, I glare at Kyon, seeing him wrap the end of my sheet around his hand.<br />"You didn't ask me what you should wear," he says in a stern tone. </b><br /><br /><br />Kyon's "love" of Kricket is pure domination:<br /><br /><b>"You think you have me tamed, Kyon?"<br />Kyon turns with a cold look in his eyes. "I plan to bring you to your knees again, Kricket." </b><br />-----------------------------------<br /><b>I narrow my eyes at him. "We're not a couple."<br />He frowns. "We <i>are</i> a couple."<br />"I don't want to be claimed."<br />"You have no say in the matter." </b><br /><br />This is <i>not okay</i>. This is not behavior that elicits a strong, healthy, romantic relationship. <b>THIS IS ABUSE, AND IF YOU SAW YOUR SISTER, OR YOUR BEST FRIEND BEING TREATED THIS WAY YOU WOULD NOT BE OKAY WITH IT. </b> I can't fucking believe that this is from a major publisher and that they're endorsing this shit. What the fuck are you telling girls who read YA? The ones who are still figuring out their self-esteem, who need to be built up? <i>Will you break them down by telling them it is okay to be hit, to be sexually molested? That it's okay to be submissive and compliant and stay with the boy who treats them this way?</i><br /><br /><u>The worst part is that Kricket falls in love with him.</u> After everything he has pulled, everything he has done to show blatant disrespect and total disregard for her:<br /><br /><i>A part of me wants to follow him. We're supposed to be a team in this.<br /><br />"You promised me a dance."<br />"I did?"<br />"Yeah, you did," I saw with a smile.</i><br /><br />I am so repulsed. I am disgusted and can't seem to shake the nasty feeling I have after finishing this book. I HAVE SO MUCH AMMO THAT PROVES HOW ABUSIVE KYON IS. How do you justify this treatment? How do you look at a 14-year-old and tell her this is okay? <b>I would <u>never</u> let my younger sister read this trash.</b> There are legitimately good books out there, and this is not one. </span>

<div id="review_1356232006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1356232006" />
    <a title="Ana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4593305-ana"><img alt="Ana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1290988959p2/4593305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1356232006?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana" href="/user/show/4593305-ana">Ana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1356232006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2762259110469975233">5 *wow that was intense* stars!!! I finished this book several days ago and my feelings are still raw. I feel like I don’t have the words (as I stare at my mostly blank computer screen) to convey how this book pleased me, saddened me, and made me fall in love with this world all over again. So many secrets are shared, so many story lines unraveled, and so many characters surprised me. From the very first page, I was lost to this amazing world that Ms. Bartol has created and I’m not sorry that I </span>
  <span id="freeText2762259110469975233" style="display:none">5 *wow that was intense* stars!!! I finished this book several days ago and my feelings are still raw. I feel like I don’t have the words (as I stare at my mostly blank computer screen) to convey how this book pleased me, saddened me, and made me fall in love with this world all over again. So many secrets are shared, so many story lines unraveled, and so many characters surprised me. From the very first page, I was lost to this amazing world that Ms. Bartol has created and I’m not sorry that I traded sleep for the opportunity to spend every possible moment immersed in this story.<br /><br />I love that Kricket really came into her own here. She’s always been an intelligent, sassy character but, in this book, she’s fierce. She’s not afraid to take on the challenges before her, she’s not afraid to make decisions that may surprise you, and, most of all, she’s not afraid to open her heart in some unlikely ways. As the pieces of her destiny come together, she struggles to find the answers but never gives up. She’s strong and she untimely has to make sacrifices…ones I didn’t see coming!<br /><br />Now, if you haven’t read the book yet, what I’m about to tell you may be a bit of a *SPOILER*…so proceed with caution!!<br /><br />Are you still here?!?! If you are, I must tell you that among all the emotions that I felt in this book, one was a very big surprise to me and I’m still wondering how Amy Bartol managed to make me do something I didn’t think I would ever do again. You see, a few years ago I read a wonderful series that many of you have probably read as well (*waves hello to the lovely Tahereh Mafi*) and during that series, I abandoned my team (*hangs head in shame*…well, not really). You see, by end of her series, I was head over heels for the bad guy. But, that was a one-time thing I told myself…it’ll never happen again. Then along came Kyon. Yes, Kyon. And once again, I have to say that I’m abandoning my previous #TeamTrey status. I’m turning in my membership card and moving on because, as Kricket discovered more about Kyon, so did I. And I just couldn’t help myself, I fell for him. Yes, he’s still rough around the edges, easy to anger and a little full of himself. But, gosh, his protectiveness towards Kricket and his focus on her is so overwhelming that I just couldn’t help myself. So much so that I sent my blog mate Christina this text…<br /><br /> “Are you flailing over Kyon? Please tell me you are…<br /> tell me I’m not alone!!!<br /> It’s Warner all over again for me!!<br /> #gottalovethebadboy”<br /><br />So…there you have it. I loved this book and I loved Kyon. You’ll probably read some reviews that focus on the end of this book (an ending which some will love, some will hate and some, like me, will pray is not really the end) but I’d much rather focus on the amazing world building, the fantastic characters and the unexpected surprises…all of which come together to create a phenomenal series!! So, if you haven’t picked this up, you are definitely missing out. Go get it now!!!<br /><br />Then you too can join #TeamKyon!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2762259110469975233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1345061072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1345061072" />
    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3335620-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473687033p2/3335620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1345061072?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/3335620-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335620-christina?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335620-christina?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335620-christina?shelf=own-on-nook-kindle">own-on-nook-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335620-christina?shelf=indie">indie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335620-christina?shelf=heavy-on-the-swoons">heavy-on-the-swoons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335620-christina?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335620-christina?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335620-christina?shelf=series-trilogies">series-trilogies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335620-christina?shelf=i-d-marry-that-boy-or-girl">i-d-marry-that-boy-or-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335620-christina?shelf=badass-chicks-in-the-building">badass-chicks-in-the-building</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1345061072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16804050186661920790">I reviewed this title with one of my co-bloggers, Ana. Our original review of this title can be found <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24931971-darken-the-stars' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>here</b>
</a> on The Book Hookup.<br/><br/><b>**Note:</b> <i>This book was provided to the Book Hookup by the publisher via NetGalley, but that did not influence this review in any way.</i><br/><br/><b>Ana: 5 *wow that was intense* stars!!!</b> I finished this book several days ago and my feelings are still raw. I feel like I don't have the words (as I stare at my mostly blank computer screen) to convey how this book pleased me, saddened me</span>
  <span id="freeText16804050186661920790" style="display:none">I reviewed this title with one of my co-bloggers, Ana. Our original review of this title can be found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24931971-darken-the-stars" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>here</b>
</a> on The Book Hookup.<br /><br /><b>**Note:</b> <i>This book was provided to the Book Hookup by the publisher via NetGalley, but that did not influence this review in any way.</i><br /><br /><b>Ana: 5 *wow that was intense* stars!!!</b> I finished this book several days ago and my feelings are still raw. I feel like I don't have the words (as I stare at my mostly blank computer screen) to convey how this book pleased me, saddened me, and made me fall in love with this world all over again. So many secrets are shared, so many story lines unraveled, and so many characters surprised me. From the very first page, I was lost to this amazing world that Ms. Bartol has created and I'm not sorry that I traded sleep for the opportunity to spend every possible moment immersed in this story.<br /><br />I love that Kricket really came into her own here. She's always been an intelligent, sassy character but, in this book, she's fierce. She's not afraid to take on the challenges before her, she's not afraid to make decisions that may surprise you, and, most of all, she's not afraid to open her heart in some unlikely ways. As the pieces of her destiny come together, she struggles to find the answers but never gives up. She's strong and she untimely has to make sacrifices...ones I didn't see coming!<br /><br />Now, if you haven't read the book yet, what I'm about to tell you may be a bit of a *SPOILER*...so proceed with caution!!<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Are you still here?!?! If you are, I must tell you that among all the emotions that I felt in this book, one was a very big surprise to me and I'm still wondering how Amy Bartol managed to make me do something I didn't think I would ever do again. You see, a few years ago I read a wonderful series that many of you have probably read as well (*waves hello to the lovely Tahereh Mafi*) and during that series, I abandoned my team (*hangs head in shame*...well, not really). You see, by end of her series, I was head over heels for the bad guy. But, that was a one-time thing I told myself...it'll never happen again. Then along came Kyon. Yes, Kyon. And once again, I have to say that I'm abandoning my previous #TeamTrey status. I'm turning in my membership card and moving on because, as Kricket discovered more about Kyon, so did I. And I just couldn't help myself, I fell for him. Yes, he's still rough around the edges, easy to anger and a little full of himself. But, gosh, his protectiveness towards Kricket and his focus on her is so overwhelming that I just couldn't help myself. So much so that I sent Christina this text...<br /><br /><blockquote><b>"Are you flailing over Kyon? Please tell me you are...<br />tell me I'm not alone!!!<br />It's Warner all over again for me!!<br />#gottalovethebadboy"</b></blockquote><br /><br />So...there you have it. I loved this book and I loved Kyon.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>You'll probably read some reviews that focus on the end of this book (an ending which some will love, some will hate and some, like me, will pray is not really the end) but I'd much rather focus on the amazing world building, the fantastic characters and the unexpected surprises...all of which come together to create a phenomenal series!! So, if you haven't picked this up, you are definitely missing out. Go get it now!!!<br /><br />Then you too can join #TeamKyon!!<br /><br /><b>Christina: 5 stars!</b> I don't even know where to <i>even</i> freaking start, especially after Ana already elaborated about the best parts. My thoughts are a tangled web of emotions and the more I try to unravel them, the more entrapped I become. I guess the easiest place to start is by saying this: Ms. Amy "Badass" Bartol has done it again! This woman is a world builder if I've ever read one. I always know that once I begin her stories, I'll be thrust into a new world that will undoubtedly transport my mind and be bent to her creative authorly will. I absolutely loved coming back to Ethar, and, specifically during this novel, "living" on Kyon's island in the Sea of Stars and staying on his Alameedan estate. Another thing you can count on Bartol to deliver is the action. As Kricket's story evolves, you'll find the betrayals run deeper, new scarier enemies are uncovered, and there are surprises around every corner, ones that will have you racing through the pages to see how it all works out. I always enjoy reading Bartol's books simply because just when you feel like you have discovered which way it's going to go, that theory will explode in your face and hundreds of other potential scenarios will be born in an instant. It always makes for a fascinating, thrilling journey. Aside from those other glorious factors that bring about awesome books, Bartol is also guaranteed to give you exceptional characters. Ones that will twist your heart this way and that, tug you along emotionally, as they develop until these people leap off of the page and in to your heart, leaving you feeling wrung dry and physically spent. I love watching her characters evolve as we progress through each subsequent novel, and this <i>Kricket</i> series is no different. I've thoroughly enjoyed watching Kricket grow even more into her own person, becoming even more fierce, vibrant, and bold. And, of course, if you mention Kricket, you have to mention her love interests. Yes, plural. I love the push and pull of a good triangle, and this author knows how to do them right. She takes the time to build the relationships and to show the building of that connection. I adore Trey, don't get me wrong, but I have been enthralled with Kyon from the very beginning, way back in the first novel of this series. Bartol knows how to work the mind of the anti-hero and before you have a chance to blink, you'll be ensnared in his wicked spell of doom and demise. Though her bad guys are phenomenally good at being oh so very, very bad, I love that Ms. Amy gives us the time to know them, to see their depth and development, to recognize the person beneath that "monster" façade. Kyon was the perfect portrayal of her talent in that area for me. I do love me a bad guy; the more deviously, deliciously dark, the better. (Don't judge me, it's a weakness.)<br /><br />Now for the elephant in the room (aside from the blasted love triangle other readers have no doubt ranted/raved/threw a giant hissy fit about), that traitorous ending! Spoiler alert: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[SHE CHOSE NO ONE AND WENT BACK TO EARTH ALONE! While, initially, I was super upset, I woke up this morning after a brief bit of sleep with a bit of clarity: She didn't chose no one,  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> ...she chose herself and her freedom, which is absolutely something that I can respect. Lord knows that while it has it's loose ends and storylines felt unfinished, not everything in life can be so easily gathered in starlight and sprinkled with fairy dust to work out perfectly, so I can appreciate this journey for what it worked itself out to be: A girl that truly found herself. That being said, which publisher person do I need to <s>beg</s> speak with to make at least one more book happen.<br /><br />As always, thank you Ms. Bartol for giving me an epic adventure and for giving me the bad boy that others love to hate and that I... well, <i>really freaking love</i>. Those boys make my heart pitter-patter like no other, well, aside from you. *squeeeeeeze* Now, if you wanted some other priestess-- say you wanted to name her, oh, I don't know... Christina, to help Kyon mend his broken heart in the absence of Kricket, well, I wouldn't hate you one bit for it. *cough*Pretty please make this happen. At least for me. You can send it directly to my inbox.*cough*<br /><br />♥ <b>A very special thanks to 47North and NetGalley for providing us with an advanced copy of this title in exchange for our honest review.</b></span>

<div id="review_1223902948" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1223902948" />
    <a title="Patricia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17541346-patricia"><img alt="Patricia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514823759p2/17541346.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1223902948?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patricia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patricia " href="/user/show/17541346-patricia">Patricia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1223902948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12304043579066604017">Darken The Stars is a tumultuous journey of self-preservation where illusions of love will reconstruct your beliefs in what happily-ever-after really encompasses. <br/><br/>This is one of the most difficult reviews I have ever written. I have spent the better part of the last 8 days mulling over the story and trying to get a handle on my emotions. I have chatted with my book friends and engaged other readers in discussion in the hopes that I might find something that would make me feel better. Unfortunate</span>
  <span id="freeText12304043579066604017" style="display:none">Darken The Stars is a tumultuous journey of self-preservation where illusions of love will reconstruct your beliefs in what happily-ever-after really encompasses. <br /><br />This is one of the most difficult reviews I have ever written. I have spent the better part of the last 8 days mulling over the story and trying to get a handle on my emotions. I have chatted with my book friends and engaged other readers in discussion in the hopes that I might find something that would make me feel better. Unfortunately, that is not the case and so I am going to attempt to address some of the issues that lead to my rating. <br /><br />Character consistency is something that is definitely hard to maintain throughout a series. I don’t envy authors who have to balance character growth among the myriad of other elements of writing to create a story that is well written and keeps the reader engaged. I don’t feel like character consistency was achieved in this book because the Kricket and Trey I fell in love with in the first two books were almost unrecognizable in Darken the Stars. <br /><br />I was captivated by these characters and truly believed that Kricket was the most determined heroine I had ever encountered. This snippet from the synopsis perfectly describes the Kricket I was expecting to see in DTS. <br /><br />“…she has an unbreakable desire to live life on her own terms, a life that she desperately wants to share with her love, Trey Allairis” – Synopsis for DTS<br /><br />But this Kricket shook my belief. It was as if she had been broken and lost her will to really live and succumbed to the powers others exerted over her. What happened to the fighter? I have no doubt she had to make difficult choices to survive under the circumstances and with all the new information that came to light. But she felt like a shell of the Kricket I love. <br /><br />While there were glimpses of the Trey I had come to love, this Trey felt like an imposter to me. What happened to the Rafe soldier who would do whatever it took to protect Kricket? I miss the man who loved with such all-consuming passion; the man who abandoned his duties to his people to protect those he loves. <br />*<br />*<br />*<br />*<br />*<br />*<br />***********POSSIBLE SPOILERS BEYOND THIS POINT**************<br />I generally strive to keep my reviews spoiler free. But I have an overwhelming need to address some of the things that just did not work for me with DTS.<br /><br />There was a chemistry between Trey and Kricket from the beginning. That chemistry escalated into an EPIC love story that complemented Kricket’s riveting adventures on Ethar. I realize there is so much more to this story than Kricket’s love life, but I can’t help but feel cheated with the way the series concludes. I most definitely have a new appreciate for Kyon and that surprised me given that I despised him in the first two books. But I never felt that Kyon and Kricket shared a connection that was remotely close to what Trey and Kricket shared. <br /><br />“You cannot thrive under the wrong stars, Kricket” - it all comes back to that statement courtesy of Trey in Under Different Stars. Whether the correct stars are on Earth or Ethar, makes no difference to me. But the ending leaves so much unresolved conflict and the illusion of a HEA (Happily Ever After), when in reality it felt more like a HFN (Happy For Now). <br /><br />Kricket has endured so much on this journey and I refuse to believe her story ends here. She is destined for so much more – I can feel it in my bones and I hope that I will have the opportunity to see that play out. If this is truly how the series ends, then I am sad to say this did not work for me because I have absolutely no closure with these characters or this story. <br /><br />I received a complimentary copy from the publisher in exchange for an honest review. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12304043579066604017" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7yCC6rYAeSknBVhe539+1AIK2EpmsanmYSflLDSUGxGo/k6jDmKaUxmHKNeF59lsJrThL1QQjEAxSXUpsKuntQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EMcHWjSbkpccLn76NarOJU/ISLrU8YaEuC6N9/YcHkdXGcsTjPlx7SKsDnNXMmmda3Zx3+ZQoyLoQB3yciOi4w==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText1834898841406668901" style="display:none">Author of the Secondborn Series:<br />Secondborn (Book 1)<br />Traitor Born (Book 2)<br />Rebel Born (Book 3) <br /><br />Author of the Premonition Series:<br />Inescapable (Book 1) <br />Intuition (Book 2)<br />Indebted (Book 3)<br />Incendiary (Book 4) <br />Iniquity (Book 5) <br /><br />Author of the Kricket Series:<br />Under Different Stars (Book 1) <br />Sea of Stars (Book 2)<br />Darken the Stars (Book 3)<br /><br />The Divided - A Science Fiction Romance short story, which is included in the Take Me To Your Reader: An Otherworld Anthology. <br /><br />Amy A. Bartol is the USA Today and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of The Secondborn Series, The Premonition Series, The Kricket Series, and a short story entitled “The Divided.” She has won numerous awards for her writing and been nominated for several more. She's a graduate of Hillsdale College, which inspired the setting of her Premonition Series. Amy lives in Michigan with her husband and two sons, but she travels often, sparking her imagination to create more worlds like the ones with hidden angels, doorways to alien landscapes, and fantastical futuristic societies and technologies. To learn more, visit Amy's website at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.amyabartol.com">https://www.amyabartol.com</a></span>
